Creation of API KEY:

For this assignment firstly, I have visited https://developer.nytimes.com/ website to create an accoun with NYT devlopers website.I have also registered an app named Ranalysis to get my API key.After acquiring the key,I have used it too look for the news article on the new COVID 19 variants.I have worked with Mike Kearneys nytimes package to get access to the Article Search API. jsonlite is also implemented to read in the json data and transform into in a R dataframe.

library(jsonlite)
library(tidyverse)

Extracting Data:

Term, begin date , end date parameters were created to access data.The date is formatted in YYYYMMDD. Term refers to the COVID variant news artcle.

term <- "COVID variant" # Need to use + to string together separate words
begin_date <- str_replace_all(Sys.Date()-7, "-", "")
end_date <- str_replace_all(Sys.Date(), "-", "")

A value named baseurl is created. after that the query was pasted with parameters and my API key to fetch articles regarding new COVID 19 variant.

baseurl <- paste0("http://api.nytimes.com/svc/search/v2/articlesearch.json?q=",term,
                  "&begin_date=",begin_date,"&end_date=",end_date,
                  "&facet_filter=true&api-key=GOnSpbnTPil1XnvQ7BolKxAhE2LVH4bQ",sep="")
initialQuery <- fromJSON(baseurl)
maxPages <- round((initialQuery$response$meta$hits[1] / 10)-1)

A for loop is set to to loop through 0 to maximum pages. The maximum page has been set to 2.For each page a data frame is created by querying the baseurl and pasting on the page number.

pages <- list()
for(i in 0:2){
  nytSearch <- fromJSON(paste0(baseurl, "&page=", i), flatten = TRUE) %>% data.frame() 
  message("Retrieving page ", i)
  pages[[i+1]] <- nytSearch 
  Sys.sleep(1) 
}
## Retrieving page 0
## Retrieving page 1
## Retrieving page 2

Transformatin to R data frame:

After retrieving pages, all of them are combined into one dataframe.

covidvariantdf <- rbind_pages(pages) 
print(paste0("we have successfully scrapped ", dim(covidvariantdf)[1], " articles about new COVID variant"))
## [1] "we have successfully scrapped 30 articles about new COVID variant"

view(covidvariantdf) %>% kable() %>% 
  kable_styling(bootstrap_options = "striped", font_size = 10) %>% 
  scroll_box(height = "500px", width = "100%")

Says U.K. Variant Is Now Most Common in the U.S. NA NA NA NA NA NA By The Associated Press NULL The Associated Press 54 0 21
OK Copyright (c) 2021 The New York Times Company. All Rights Reserved. The B.1.1.7 variant, first identified in Britain, is now the source of most new coronavirus infections in the United States, the director of the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention said. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/07/us/politics/coronavirus-variants-cdc.html The B.1.1.7 variant, first identified in Britain, is now the source of most new coronavirus infections in the United States, the director of the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention said. WASHINGTON A highly infectious variant of the coronavirus that was first identified in Britain has become the most common source of new infections in the United States, the director of the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention said on Wednesday. The worrisome development comes as officials and scientists warn of a possible fourth surge of infections. Researchers are scrambling to assess whether new coronavirus variants are playing a role in India. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/09/world/asia/india-covid-vaccine-variant.html The new wave will hurt global efforts and vaccine supplies, experts say. Researchers are scrambling to assess whether new coronavirus variants are playing a role in India. NEW DELHI When the coronavirus first struck India last year, the country enforced one of the worlds strictest national lockdowns. The warning was clear: A fast spread in a population of 1.3 billion would be devastating. nyt://article/991951c4-62e3-512f-b4a7-aa2d4bd84a0c A 1 Asia Pacific Complacency and Missteps Deepen a Covid-19 Crisis in India NA NA Complacency Deepens a Virus Disaster in India NA NA NA By Mujib Pediatricians should be vigilant, experts said, after the release of the largest U.S. study of the syndrome, MIS-C, that can strike young people weeks after their coronavirus infection. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/06/health/covid-children-mis-c.html Pediatricians should be vigilant, experts said, after the release of the largest U.S. study of the syndrome, MIS-C, that can strike young people weeks after their coronavirus infection. Many children and teenagers who developed the mysterious inflammatory syndrome that can emerge several weeks after contracting the coronavirus never had classic Covid-19 symptoms at the time of their infection, according to the largest study so far of cases in the United States. nyt://interactive/564eb8b1-42d2-5eba-8f03-b22a557396fc MM 32 NA How the Skagit Valley Chorale Learned to Sing Again Amid Covid NA NA Voices Carry NA NA NA By Kim Tingley Kim , NA , Tingley , NA , NA , Stretching the time between the first and second doses would greatly accelerate the rate at which people get at least partial protection. But some experts fear it could also lead to new variants. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/09/health/covid-vaccine-second-dose-delay.html Stretching the time between the first and second doses would greatly accelerate the rate at which people get at least partial protection. But some experts fear it could also lead to new variants. The prospect of a fourth wave of the coronavirus, with new cases climbing sharply in the Upper Midwest, has reignited a debate among vaccine experts over how long to wait between the first and second doses. Extending that period would swiftly increase the number of people with the partial protection of a single shot, but some experts fear it could also give rise to dangerous new variants. When asked why his state wasnt seeing higher reported cases after removing restrictions, the Texas governor speculated that the population had reached herd immunity. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/11/world/texas-herd-immunity-governor.html When asked why his state wasnt seeing higher reported cases after removing restrictions, the Texas governor speculated that the population had reached herd immunity. Gov.Greg Abbott of Texas may have been overly optimistic on Sunday when he said on Fox News that his state could be very close to herd immunity the point where so much of the population is immune to Covid-19, either from being vaccinated or previously infected, that the virus can no longer spread. At least 16 players and a coach are on the N.H.L.s Covid-19 protocol list, and the team has postponed four games because of the virus. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/05/sports/hockey/hockey-canucks-covid.html At least 16 players and a coach are on the N.H.L.s Covid-19 protocol list, and the team has postponed four games because of the virus. VANCOUVER, British Columbia The N.H.L.s Covid-19 protocols have sidelined more than half of the Vancouver Canucks, as well as one member of the coaching staff, an extraordinary impact of the coronavirus on a sports team. India has become the epicenter of the coronavirus outbreak. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/09/us/coronavirus-today.html India has become the epicenter of the coronavirus outbreak. India has become the epicenter of the coronavirus outbreak, reporting a record of 131,968 new cases in the last 24 hours as the virus spins out of control. Deaths are rising, hospitals are quickly filling up and the countrys vaccination campaign is perilously behind schedule. The president pushed up his target date by two weeks, matching the timetable already being put in place by many states. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/06/us/politics/biden-vaccine-all-adults-eligible.html The president pushed up his target date by two weeks, matching the timetable already being put in place by many states. WASHINGTON President Biden on Tuesday moved up by two weeks, to April 19, his deadline for states to make every American adult eligible for coronavirus vaccination, following the lead of states around the country that are already meeting that timetable. Biden Moves Up Deadline for Vaccine Eligibility NA NA NA By Sheryl Gay Stolberg Sheryl , Gay , Stolberg, NA , NA , reported, , 1 NA 54 10 16
OK Copyright (c) 2021 The New York Times Company. All Rights Reserved. Much of the continent remains closed to Americans because of the virus, but many travelers want to visit this summer. Will their plans materialize? https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/09/travel/vacation-summer-europe.html Much of the continent remains closed to Americans because of the virus, but many travelers want to visit this summer. Will their plans materialize? My husband and I are currently planning a trip to Ireland, Portugal and Italy for August and September. We are only reserving hotels with free cancellation policies and our airline tickets can be changed to a future date. Knowing that much of Europe is closed right now to United States citizens because of the virus, is there much hope that our plans will materialize, or are we wasting our time? What should I watch for? High-profile arrests rock Jordan. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/04/briefing/jordan-taliban-negotiations.html High-profile arrests rock Jordan. The Jordanian government has arrested high-profile figures, including Sharif Hassan bin Zaid, a member of the royal family, and Bassem Awadallah, a former chief of the royal court, an unusual development in the normally stable Arab kingdom. Officials cited the security and stability of Jordan as reasons for the moves. Vaccine passports are shaping up to be the next big wedge issue in the United States. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/06/us/coronavirus-today-vaccines.html Vaccine passports are shaping up to be the next big wedge issue in the United States. As the ranks of the inoculated in the U.S. grow, businesses, schools and politicians are considering vaccine passports digital proof of vaccination against the coronavirus as a path to reviving the economy and postpandemic life. Gov.Gretchen Whitmer, a Democrat, said she had pushed the president unsuccessfully to send more vaccines to her state, where hospitals are filling. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/09/us/michigan-covid-vaccine.html Gov.Gretchen Whitmer, a Democrat, said she had pushed the president unsuccessfully to send more vaccines to her state, where hospitals are filling. Gov.Gretchen Whitmer of Michigan said Friday that she had urged President Biden to surge Covid-19 vaccines into her state, where a worst-in-the-nation outbreak has filled hospitals and forced some schools to close. Four million is the new benchmark for the U.S. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/06/briefing/three-million-daily-shots-achieved.html And now? Four million is the new benchmark for the U.S. Shortly after President Biden took office, I began asking his aides why their publicly announced goal for Covid-19 vaccine distribution an average of one million shots a day was so unambitious. The pace wasnt much faster than what the Trump administration had achieved in its final days, and it was far short of the rate at which vaccine makers would be delivering doses to the government. Based on that delivery schedule, a reasonable goal seemed to be three million shots a day. The economy has almost fully reopened. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/05/world/israel-offers-a-hint-of-what-post-pandemic-life-may-look-like.html Israels vaccination program has been remarkably swift and successful. In recent weeks, new coronavirus infections have dropped significantly, from a peak of 10,000 a day in January to a few hundred by late March. The economy has almost fully reopened. offers a hint of what post-pandemic life may look like. NA NA NA NA NA NA By Isabel Kershner Isabel , NA , Kershner, NA , NA , reported, , 1 NA 54 20 16

The global economy is expected to expand by 6 percent this year, up from a previous projection of 5.5 percent, after a contraction of 3.3 percent in 2020. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/06/business/imf-outlook-global-economy.html The global economy is expected to expand by 6 percent this year, up from a previous projection of 5.5 percent, after a contraction of 3.3 percent in 2020. The global economy is recovering from the coronavirus pandemic faster than previously expected, largely thanks to the strength of the United States, but the International Monetary Fund warned on Tuesday that major challenges remained as the uneven rollout of vaccines threatens to leave developing countries behind. The I.M.F. sees a faster economic recovery as vaccines are deployed. OK Copyright (c) 2021 The New York Times Company. All Rights Reserved. Millions of white evangelical adults in the U.S. do not intend to get vaccinated against Covid-19. Tenets of faith and mistrust of science play a role; so does politics. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/05/us/covid-vaccine-evangelicals.html Millions of white evangelical adults in the U.S. do not intend to get vaccinated against Covid-19. Tenets of faith and mistrust of science play a role; so does politics. Stephanie Nana, an evangelical Christian in Edmond, Okla., refused to get a Covid-19 vaccine because she believed it contained aborted cell tissue. The extraordinary move came just days after officials learned the plant had ruined 15 million doses of Johnson & Johnsons coronavirus vaccine. https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/03/us/politics/emergent-vaccine-plant-johnson-johnson.html The extraordinary move came just days after officials learned the plant had ruined 15 million doses of Johnson & Johnsons coronavirus vaccine. WASHINGTON The Biden administration on Saturday put Johnson & Johnson in charge of a troubled Baltimore manufacturing plant that ruined 15 million doses of the Johnson & Johnson coronavirus vaccine and moved to stop the plant from making another vaccine by AstraZeneca, senior federal health officials said. Barplot:

The barplot refelects new COVID variants are mostly discussed in news articles.

covidvariantdf%>% 
  group_by(response.docs.type_of_material) %>%
  summarize(count=n()) %>%
  mutate(percent = (count / sum(count))*100) %>%
  ggplot() +
  geom_bar(aes(y=percent, x=response.docs.type_of_material, fill=response.docs.type_of_material), stat = "identity")
